   for lists of user-defined sorts. \K 's builtin way of doing this is to use
   List\{KItem,"Separator"\}, where "Separator" is any valid character or
   sequence of characters used to separate distinct elements.
   For example, after defining \\
   syntax KItem ::= Elt\\
   a user could then define
   syntax Elts ::= List\{Elt,","\} \\
   which would be a comma-separated list whose elements are all of sort Elt. A
   user could just as well define \\
   syntax Elts ::= List\{Elt,"and"\} \\
   which would be a list containing elements of sort Elt that are separated with
   the word "and". If only one argument is given, the separator is asumed to be
   commas. So, \\
   syntax Elts = List\{Elt\} \\
   would define a comma-separated list containing elements of sort Elt.
  ,[UNIQUE_ID(a2062c4827a4896f45d92f547367109710ed3635f3f60b49c23460811897cc29) org.kframework.attributes.Location(Location(219,3,235,4)) org.kframework.attributes.Source(Source(/usr/lib/kframework/include/builtin/domains.k))])
  ModuleComment( \section{Description} \K lists are ordered collections that may contain
   duplicate elements. These behave more like lists in functional programming
   languages than arrays in imperative programming languages; there's no
   numerical indexing, but instead specific elements are refered to using the
   Mylist,Mylist construct in combination with the MyListItem construct. It's
   worth noting that \K lists aren't exactly like lists in functional languages;
   they're associative, which means that it's easy to access elements at both
   ends of the lists and concatenate them. For example, L:Mylist,E accesses
   element E at the end of a list. ,[UNIQUE_ID(8e2817619363882be8e8a58585b09b99206a0973ff9b9308e6a486a54e8d337b) org.kframework.attributes.Location(Location(208,3,216,37)) org.kframework.attributes.Source(Source(/usr/lib/kframework/include/builtin/domains.k))])

  ModuleComment( \section{User-Defined Lists} It is very common in \K to define a shorthand
   for lists of user-defined sorts. \K 's builtin way of doing this is to use
   List\{KItem,"Separator"\}, where "Separator" is any valid character or
   sequence of characters used to separate distinct elements.
   For example, after defining \\
   syntax KItem ::= Elt\\
   a user could then define
   syntax Elts ::= List\{Elt,","\} \\
   which would be a comma-separated list whose elements are all of sort Elt. A
   user could just as well define \\
   syntax Elts ::= List\{Elt,"and"\} \\
   which would be a list containing elements of sort Elt that are separated with
   the word "and". If only one argument is given, the separator is asumed to be
   commas. So, \\
   syntax Elts = List\{Elt\} \\
   would define a comma-separated list containing elements of sort Elt.
  ,[UNIQUE_ID(a2062c4827a4896f45d92f547367109710ed3635f3f60b49c23460811897cc29) org.kframework.attributes.Location(Location(219,3,235,4)) org.kframework.attributes.Source(Source(/usr/lib/kframework/include/builtin/domains.k))])
  ModuleComment( \section{Description} \K lists are ordered collections that may contain
   duplicate elements. These behave more like lists in functional programming
   languages than arrays in imperative programming languages; there's no
   numerical indexing, but instead specific elements are refered to using the
   Mylist,Mylist construct in combination with the MyListItem construct. It's
   worth noting that \K lists aren't exactly like lists in functional languages;
   they're associative, which means that it's easy to access elements at both
   ends of the lists and concatenate them. For example, L:Mylist,E accesses
   element E at the end of a list. ,[UNIQUE_ID(8e2817619363882be8e8a58585b09b99206a0973ff9b9308e6a486a54e8d337b) org.kframework.attributes.Location(Location(208,3,216,37)) org.kframework.attributes.Source(Source(/usr/lib/kframework/include/builtin/domains.k))])

  ModuleComment(
// Q: Expressions patterns?
  syntax              Exp ::= "{" Exp "}" [bracket]
                            | AExp
                            | StringExp
                            > BExp


// Arithmetic
  syntax         IntOrVar ::= Int | ProcVar | Eval
  syntax             AExp ::= "{" AExp "}" [bracket]
                            > IntOrVar
                            > "-" AExp       [strict]
                            > AExp "%" AExp  [strict] // mod reduction
                            > AExp "*" AExp  [strict, left]
                            | AExp "/" AExp  [strict, left]
                            > AExp "+" AExp  [strict, left]
                            | AExp "-" AExp  [strict, left]

// String
  syntax      StringOrVar ::= String | ProcVar | Eval
  syntax        StringExp ::= "{" StringExp "}" [bracket]
                            > StringOrVar
                            | Concat  // string concatenation
                            | Interp  // string interpolation: "${key}rest" %% { key:value , ... } => "value" ++ "rest"

  syntax           Concat ::= StringOrVar ConcatExp
  syntax        ConcatExp ::= "++" StringOrVar
                            | "++" StringOrVar ConcatExp

  syntax           Interp ::= StringOrVar "%%" InterpMaps
  syntax       InterpMaps ::= RhoMap
                            | RhoMap "%%" InterpMaps

// Boolean
  syntax             BExp ::= "{" BExp "}"   [bracket]
                            > Bool                // boolean output
                            | ProcVar             // e.g. \x == Proc or not \x
                            | Eval                // e.g. *x == Proc or not *x
                            > AExp "<=" AExp      [seqstrict]
                            | AExp "<"  AExp      [seqstrict]
                            | AExp ">=" AExp      [seqstrict]
                            > AExp ">"  AExp      [seqstrict]
                            | Name "==" Name      // name equivalence
                            | Name "!=" Name      // not ( Name == Name )
                            | Proc "==" Proc      // structural equivalence
                            | Proc "!=" Proc      // not ( Proc == Proc )
                            > "not" BExp          [strict]
                            > BExp "and" BExp     [strict(1), right]
                            > BExp "or"  BExp     [strict(1), right]
                            > Proc "matches" Proc // P matches Q is syntactic sugar for: match P { { Q :=> true } { P :=> false } }

// Q: Bundle patterns?
  syntax           Bundle ::= "bundle+" "{" ProcPat "}"   // write-only
                            | "bundle-" "{" ProcPat "}"   // read-only
                            | "bundle0" "{" ProcPat "}"   // neither read/write
                            | "bundle"  "{" ProcPat "}"   // both read/write

// Q: Method patterns?

                            | ProcPat MethodAndArgs
                            | ProcPat MethArgPats
  syntax    NEMethArgPats ::= "." Method "(" ProcPats ")"
                            | "." Method "(" ProcPat  ")"
  syntax      MethArgPats ::= NEMethArgPats
                            | "." Method "(" ")"

module AUXFUN-SYNTAX$SYNTAX [org.kframework.attributes.Location(Location(14,1,115,9)) org.kframework.attributes.Source(Source(/home/isaac/Documents/KFramework/Git-clone/KFramework/Languages/GroundedRho/AuxFun/auxfun.k))]

  syntax String ::= "#interpolate(" String ";" RhoMap ")"
  syntax Set ::= "#par2Set(" Proc ")"
  syntax RhoSet ::= "#union(" RhoSet ";" RhoSet ")"
  syntax RhoSet ::= "#keys(" RhoMap ")"
  syntax RhoList ::= "#truncate(" RhoList "," Int ")"
  syntax RhoList ::= "#slice(" RhoList "," Int "," Int ")"
  syntax RhoKVPairs ::= "#append(" RhoKVPairs ";" RhoKVPairs ")"
  syntax RhoKVPairs ::= "#append(" RhoKVPairs ";" RhoKVPair ")"
  syntax RhoKVPairs ::= "#append(" RhoKVPair ";" RhoKVPairs ")"
  syntax RhoKVPairs ::= "#append(" RhoKVPair ";" RhoKVPair ")"

  ModuleComment( \section{User-Defined Lists} It is very common in \K to define a shorthand
   for lists of user-defined sorts. \K 's builtin way of doing this is to use
   List\{KItem,"Separator"\}, where "Separator" is any valid character or
   sequence of characters used to separate distinct elements.
   For example, after defining \\
   syntax KItem ::= Elt\\
   a user could then define
   syntax Elts ::= List\{Elt,","\} \\
   which would be a comma-separated list whose elements are all of sort Elt. A
   user could just as well define \\
   syntax Elts ::= List\{Elt,"and"\} \\
   which would be a list containing elements of sort Elt that are separated with
   the word "and". If only one argument is given, the separator is asumed to be
   commas. So, \\
   syntax Elts = List\{Elt\} \\
   would define a comma-separated list containing elements of sort Elt.
  ,[UNIQUE_ID(a2062c4827a4896f45d92f547367109710ed3635f3f60b49c23460811897cc29) org.kframework.attributes.Location(Location(219,3,235,4)) org.kframework.attributes.Source(Source(/usr/lib/kframework/include/builtin/domains.k))])
  ModuleComment( \section{Description} \K lists are ordered collections that may contain
   duplicate elements. These behave more like lists in functional programming
   languages than arrays in imperative programming languages; there's no
   numerical indexing, but instead specific elements are refered to using the
   Mylist,Mylist construct in combination with the MyListItem construct. It's
   worth noting that \K lists aren't exactly like lists in functional languages;

  ModuleComment(
// Q: Expressions patterns?
  syntax              Exp ::= "{" Exp "}" [bracket]
                            | AExp
                            | StringExp
                            > BExp


// Arithmetic
  syntax         IntOrVar ::= Int | ProcVar | Eval
  syntax             AExp ::= "{" AExp "}" [bracket]
                            > IntOrVar
                            > "-" AExp       [strict]
                            > AExp "%" AExp  [strict] // mod reduction
                            > AExp "*" AExp  [strict, left]
                            | AExp "/" AExp  [strict, left]
                            > AExp "+" AExp  [strict, left]
                            | AExp "-" AExp  [strict, left]

// String
  syntax      StringOrVar ::= String | ProcVar | Eval
  syntax        StringExp ::= "{" StringExp "}" [bracket]
                            > StringOrVar
                            | Concat  // string concatenation
                            | Interp  // string interpolation: "${key}rest" %% { key:value , ... } => "value" ++ "rest"

  syntax           Concat ::= StringOrVar ConcatExp
  syntax        ConcatExp ::= "++" StringOrVar
                            | "++" StringOrVar ConcatExp

  syntax           Interp ::= StringOrVar "%%" InterpMaps
  syntax       InterpMaps ::= RhoMap
                            | RhoMap "%%" InterpMaps

// Boolean
  syntax             BExp ::= "{" BExp "}"   [bracket]
                            > Bool                // boolean output
                            | ProcVar             // e.g. \x == Proc or not \x
                            | Eval                // e.g. *x == Proc or not *x
                            > AExp "<=" AExp      [seqstrict]
                            | AExp "<"  AExp      [seqstrict]
                            | AExp ">=" AExp      [seqstrict]
                            > AExp ">"  AExp      [seqstrict]
                            | Name "==" Name      // name equivalence
                            | Name "!=" Name      // not ( Name == Name )
                            | Proc "==" Proc      // structural equivalence
                            | Proc "!=" Proc      // not ( Proc == Proc )
                            > "not" BExp          [strict]
                            > BExp "and" BExp     [strict(1), right]
                            > BExp "or"  BExp     [strict(1), right]
                            > Proc "matches" Proc // P matches Q is syntactic sugar for: match P { { Q :=> true } { P :=> false } }

// Q: Bundle patterns?
  syntax           Bundle ::= "bundle+" "{" ProcPat "}"   // write-only
                            | "bundle-" "{" ProcPat "}"   // read-only
                            | "bundle0" "{" ProcPat "}"   // neither read/write
                            | "bundle"  "{" ProcPat "}"   // both read/write

// Q: Method patterns?
  syntax          MethPat ::= Proc    NEMethArgPats
                            | ProcPat MethodAndArgs
                            | ProcPat MethArgPats
  syntax    NEMethArgPats ::= "." Method "(" ProcPats ")"
                            | "." Method "(" ProcPat  ")"
  syntax      MethArgPats ::= NEMethArgPats
                            | "." Method "(" ")"
,[UNIQUE_ID(df3359777c107b65b619c6ad07e41aa107fda35dd80fb7b8aca50e129aa24caa) org.kframework.attributes.Location(Location(549,1,615,2)) org.kframework.attributes.Source(Source(/home/isaac/Documents/KFramework/Git-clone/KFramework/Languages/GroundedRho/grho.k))])
  ModuleComment(
  // Process maps
  syntax           RhoMap ::= "{" RhoKVPairs "}"
                            | "{" RhoKVPair  "}"
                            | "{" "}"

  syntax        RhoKVPair ::= Proc ":" Proc
  syntax       RhoKVPairs ::= RhoKVPair "," RhoKVPair
                            | RhoKVPair "," RhoKVPairs

  syntax           RhoSet ::= "Set(" Procs ")"

                            | "Set(" ")"

module LIST [org.kframework.attributes.Location(Location(202,1,267,9)) org.kframework.attributes.Source(Source(/usr/lib/kframework/include/builtin/domains.k))]
  imports LIST$SYNTAX
  imports INT-SYNTAX
  imports BASIC-K
  ModuleComment(| ".",[UNIQUE_ID(0ce1a427591770a8b6a58775e29e4d67a3c036389798109855bea6332dbfd77a) org.kframework.attributes.Location(Location(242,17,242,24)) org.kframework.attributes.Source(Source(/usr/lib/kframework/include/builtin/domains.k))])
  ModuleComment(TODO(AndreiS): move the paragraph below,[UNIQUE_ID(d948b9104b3c9c3fe54b012ddcf9808a54f84bea3ce8d52338bb77deb806d7bd) org.kframework.attributes.Location(Location(218,3,218,44)) org.kframework.attributes.Source(Source(/usr/lib/kframework/include/builtin/domains.k))])
  ModuleComment( \section{User-Defined Lists} It is very common in \K to define a shorthand
   for lists of user-defined sorts. \K 's builtin way of doing this is to use
   List\{KItem,"Separator"\}, where "Separator" is any valid character or
   sequence of characters used to separate distinct elements.
   For example, after defining \\
   syntax KItem ::= Elt\\
   a user could then define
   syntax Elts ::= List\{Elt,","\} \\
   which would be a comma-separated list whose elements are all of sort Elt. A
   user could just as well define \\
   syntax Elts ::= List\{Elt,"and"\} \\
   which would be a list containing elements of sort Elt that are separated with
   the word "and". If only one argument is given, the separator is asumed to be
   commas. So, \\
   syntax Elts = List\{Elt\} \\
   would define a comma-separated list containing elements of sort Elt.
  ,[UNIQUE_ID(a2062c4827a4896f45d92f547367109710ed3635f3f60b49c23460811897cc29) org.kframework.attributes.Location(Location(219,3,235,4)) org.kframework.attributes.Source(Source(/usr/lib/kframework/include/builtin/domains.k))])
  ModuleComment( \section{Description} \K lists are ordered collections that may contain
   duplicate elements. These behave more like lists in functional programming
   languages than arrays in imperative programming languages; there's no
   numerical indexing, but instead specific elements are refered to using the
   Mylist,Mylist construct in combination with the MyListItem construct. It's
   worth noting that \K lists aren't exactly like lists in functional languages;
   they're associative, which means that it's easy to access elements at both
   ends of the lists and concatenate them. For example, L:Mylist,E accesses
